The Heavens belong to the Lord, but the earth He gave over to mankind.
Ps. 115:16
It is Rosh Hashanah — the birthday of the world.
“On the seventh day God finished His work which He had been doing.”
. . But so much remains to be done.
The hungry need to be fed, the illiterate need to be taught.
The old as well as the young need to be loved.
We all need relief from the stress and anxiety of personal
and global conflicts that are ravaging us.
God is perfect. Surely He could have created a perfect world.
Why didn’t He?
He deliberately left the world unfinished because He expects each generation —
every man, woman, and child — to be His partner in the continuous act of creation.
The tradition tells us that this is what it means to be human.
God endowed us with unique gifts — perception, compassion, inventiveness.
It is our job to use them to improve the world.
We teach our children that everything they do makes a difference.
We need to start believing it about ourselves —
to act as though our actions change the world a little. Because they do.
Prayer, ritual and study can make us sensitive to moments of change and choice.
They give us a renewed vision of our goal. It is when we take that vision out into
the world — and act on it — that we really become partners in creation.
What Can We Do?
Help worthy students stay in school. Read for the blind. Tutor in over-burdened schools.
Share our talents where they are needed. We can take steps to guard the water, the air,
the soil that are entrusted to us. We can respond when people around us are in pain . . .
Visit the sick and the grieving — and really listen.
In'1 a world of gossip we can respect privacy.
In violent times we can deal gently with our children and our aged.
We can take the chance of reaching out to a stranger.
We can refuse to stand idly by while our neighbor’s blood is shed.
Wake Up.
Accept your role as a partner in creation.
Rosh Hashanah is the time and wherever you are is the place to begin.
A message from
The Jewish Theological Seminary of America
East Coast Fruit Co.
Walter Portnoy — Mrs. Louis Portnoy and Families

This Issue of the Center Yearbook
is Dedicated to:
ESTHER FISHLER
As the deadline approaches, Esther Fishier is still “on a roll.” Not
ready to finalize the Center Yearbook, she continues to clip
newspaper ads of new businesses. Still in high gear, she calls one.
They are interested but want to see the Yearbook first. Esther
immediately grabs her car keys and Yearbook and is off.
Half an hour later she returns to the Center office, bubbling and
waving a check for a full page ad from a first-time subscriber. “I make
these goals for myself,” she exclaims. “Each year I like to do better
than the last.”
Esther Fishier strikes again!
Esther Fishier
This year Esther is retiring after thirty-three years of devoted service to the Jacksonville Jewish Center.
Her long career at the Center began in the Education Department. Four years later, she was asked by Rabbi
Tofield to become involved with the finances (advertising) of the Yearbook. For fifteen years she was also
responsible for the food programs which included: Saturday luncheons for 250 youngsters, Sunday breakfast
for 90, and two suppers four nights a week for Hebrew School students. She called for minyan volunteers for
14y2 years and in addition worked on membership and finances. She has been responsible for opening new
ongoing means of revenue — wedding invitations, yarmulkes, floral contributions and more.
It is in the area of Yearbook solicitation that Esther has no rival. During her tenure, Yearbook revenues
have more than tripled. Her diligence and persistence have made this annual one of our best fund raisers.
An active Sisterhood member for over forty years, Esther has been in charge of many successful projects
— the Sisterhood Card Party being her most recent accomplishment. Many of her volunteer activities
centered around her children, Herbert and Carole, who were both very involved in all the Center’s education
and youth programs.
As a devoted member and staff person of the Center, Esther has been one of our greatest fund raisers. She
is retiring this Fall from her position at the Center office “with mixed emotions . . . (she) will always have the
Center at heart . . . and still plans to continue to be active in Sisterhood and other projects.”
This grandmother of three (Jennifer, Jonathan and Michael) can still run rings around women half her age.
Her boundless energy, her drive, her generosity to her family and friends have distinguished her as a very
“special” lady.
We express our sincere appreciation to Esther for her dedication and the “extra” effort she has given
through the years. We wish her good health and happiness.
— Editor

===== PAGE 16 =====
Rabbi’s Message: Renewing the Irreplaceable
I am prompted to the considerations that follow after reading an article in the
business section in one of the important national daily newspapers. 1 usually do
nothing more than skim the headlines of this section of the paper . . . but one item
of business interest, and I think of human interest, evoked my curiosity. 1 read
further. The article explained that one publicly owned company was resisting the
constantly depressing Dow Jones stock market average of the spring and the
summer. This company was not only holding its own against the tide of the market
— in fact, it had even shown a slight gain. The company in question was into
medical technology and the research and development of replacement parts for
the human body. I had not realized the extent to which the bionic man and woman
had become a fact of life. Companies that replace parts of the human body, for a
price, are a growth industry. Indeed substitutive medicine and replacing human parts with artificial ones has
spurned the development of a community of manufacturers that endeavor to replace what was formerly
irreplaceable. There are reports of millions of people who have had artificial parts implanted inside them. There are
artificial hips, knees, elbows, arteries, breasts, lenses, and pace makers. Even the artificial human heart has become
a “fact of life” challenge to these new creators. As medical researchers contemplate the future, they are confident
that everything in the body will ultimately be duplicated by parts flowing out of a factory.
I read the article with a mixture of fascination and disquietude. Please understand — I’m all for research in this
area. I believe it to be part of God given command to mankind to realize and develop itself to its fullest creative
potential. It is a mitzvah to prolong life. It is a mitzvah to give people second opportunities ... to bring hope and healing to
those in need of help.
The psalmist explains about God, “For You have sown this flesh; You knitted these bones in my mother’s womb; I
offer my thanks for I am astonishingly and wonderfully made.” I do not know which blessings are recited when one is
provided with an artificial limb or organ ... or frankly, to whom thanks is due. Is it the scientist? technician? medical
researcher? or the insurance company that makes it all possible? But it is not God’s honor that I am concerned with.
God wants and needs partners to further His work in every human and social sphere ... no less this area of modern
medical development.
What fills me with disquietude is that if we can replace the formerly irreplaceable . . . the limbs and organs that
sustain life . . . what shall we do for the human spirit that ails as well. Man has, not only a body, but a spirit. There is in
him a Divine flame which thinks, creates, dreams, hopes, cries . . . and prays. There is in man a need for love ... for
companionship, for a sense of dignity and worth. There is in man a need to make a difference. There is in him a talent to sing,
to soar and to celebrate the wonder of life.
Is there a company which can provide replacements of the spirit when it is deficient? Can a factory provide an
implant to those who need to be able to love? to those who hunger for beauty and long for truth? Can we ask the
researchers to look into the widespread conditions of the shriveled souls and and withered spirits of modern man
and to provide their replacement parts? Is the price too high? The technology too complex? I suspect that any
agency providing replacement of the human spirit would flourish . . . would add significantly to its own stock market
average, if given the chance.
It dawned on me ... as I read this article on the replacement of the irreplaceable that the Jewish community and
tradition has had such an agency . . . one which has flourished over these last many centuries. The time is Rosh
Hashana and Yom Kippur as representatives of each day of human life. The setting for this enterprise is the
synagogue. The human spirit cannot be replaced — it need only be renewed. We Jews call that Teshuva — the ability
to return to our fullest human dimensions in the face of all that causes the spirit to shrivel. There is an element — a
winged thing within us — an invisible, but real entity which links our life to the Eternal Spirit . . . the source of our
Being. I call it God.
Our tradition states . . . “Elohai — neshama asher natata bee — tehora hee” — “Our God the spirit and soul you
have placed within me is pure and good.” (the Siddur) Is this the real meaning of the Genesis description of God providing us
with the breath of life? I think so. I venture to suggest that though we may be able to replace those physical organs with which
we were created, we will never be able to do without that spirit which comes from God and which is our most fundamental of
human endowments. It is that human endowment which cannot be replaced. It can only be renewed.
I invite you to this renewal . . . not only during the course of the High Holy days which are upon us . . . but rather
over the course of the entire year. This is a life long process ... but one we need to seek if we are each to realize that
we are heirs to a noble tradition and that we are members of the human family.
Inge and I, and the members of our family wish you and yours a year of health, happiness, purpose, blessing,
peace and renewal. Amen
Rabbi David Gaffney

Religious Services — Traditional prayer services are held daily, morning and evening in the Witten Chapel. Friday
Family services, Sabbath and Holiday Services are observed throughout the entire year.
Personal Religious Observances — Traditional Jewish customs are observed in connection with Circumcision,
Naming of Girls, Pidyon Ha-ben, Bar Mitzvah, Bat Mitzvah, Confirmation, Marriages, Conversion to Judaism,
Bereavement.
Education — Daily Kindergarten and Nursery & Day Care with outstanding program of secular and religious
content. Hebrew school, carefully graded with intensive Hebrew content, including Jewish history and customs,
Sunday School for kindergarten, first and second grades: Solomon Schechter Day School, a graded secular and
Hebrew School, 1st through 7th grades; Hebrew High School with Pre-Jr. and Junior Congregations and Minyanaire.
Extension Services — Library, outstanding collection of juvenile and adult Jewish books; Adult Education, religious
and cultural Jewish courses; music programs of religious and cultural Jewish music; P.T.A.; Sisterhood, Ha’Rayim, a
fellowship of young families; Center Couples Club, social activities provided by Mr. and Mrs. Club, Single Adults;
Family Recreation Program (Olympic pool), summer week-days and Sundays for all ages.
Youth Activities — ATID for college age youth; United Synagogue Youth, Kadima, Chalutzim, Boy Scouts, Cub
Scouts, Girl Scouts, Brownies; Sunday Funday; athletics, programs for youth and adults; Center Day Camp and
summer program at our 36 acre site.
Family Recreation Program — Center Campsite . . . swimming, athletics, snack bar; available for members during
the summer months. Campsite includes olympic-size swimming pool, 2 tennis courts, baseball, soccer and football
fields and playground.
For additional information, call the Center office — 268-6736

Message from the Director
As we enter a New Year we have the opportunity to re-evaiuate and determine what
direction we would like to follow in the future. One question to ask — What can my
membership in the Jacksonville Jewish Center do for me? The answer — Nothing, if
you do not avail yourself of the opportunity to participate in the many diversified
activities that take place at the Center during the course of a year.
Many members are just included in the membership list in this Yearbook. Yes, you
pay your dues and you are counted, but we would like to see you face-to-face. We
would like to see you at the daily minyan, where congenial groups of men meet twice
daily. We would like to see you at Shabbat Services — a perfect place to relax in prayer,
to learn, to share and enjoy the Kiddush with old friends and meet new ones.
We would like for you to make a commitment that this year will be different. You will
serve on a committee; you will attend the Art Auction, Mazel Mania and the raffle;
participate in a Shabbaton Weekend and attend some of the many other social and
educational events that are planned; and certainly you will come to Shabbat services.
Blanche Slott
Being involved is a way of communicating, a way of sharing your talents and
receiving some benefits in exchange.
Our staff is always available to assist you at any time and all join me with
warm greetings and good wishes for a year of peace, well-being and prosperity.
Blanche Slott
Administrative Director

===== PAGE 22 =====
Where will our Synagogue be next year?
President’s Message
Dr. Joseph Honigman
And the L*RD G*D called to the man, and said to him, “Where are you?”
BERESHIT 3:9
As we begin another year, most of us feel obliged to take a personal inventory.
Sometimes such a probing self analysis is not a pleasant experience. This is
especially true when we don’t measure up well to our own tough standards.
Indeed, that is what the Torah is telling us in the story of Adam hiding in Eden
from G*D. How could Adam expect to hide from G*D? Certainly G*D knew where
Adam was hiding. The question, “Where are you?” clearly was a rhetorical one
meant for Adam’s benefit.
Adam had to stop and introspect where he was, to what point he had come, what
he had done, and what his responsibilities were.
At times, we are all Adams, hiding out and evading our responsibilities, and
refusing to make full use of our G*D given potentials, abilities and talents.
As we move into another year, it would be simple to glibly pledge to do better ... to do better as Jews, better in our
interpersonal relationships, better in our homes, our synagogue and our places of work.
But setting a new, higher standard for the coming year carries with it the obligation to measure at a later date what our
performance actually was. This year, perhaps we should all make an additional resolution. Resolve that the quality control
benchmark of our performance will be an honest appraisal by the toughest inspector of all — ourselves.
In much the same way, our Synagogue has the potential to continue to improve over the coming year. And it will
improve, if our toughest quality control inspectors — our own membership — assumes an active role in measuring their
own performances with relation to the Synagogue. Because when our Synagogue’s performance does not measure up, only
the personal efforts and financial support of an involved, committed membership is capable of making the required
improvements.
“Where will our Synagogue be next year?” That is a question that each and every one of us will have to answer honestly,
at this time, next year.
L’Shana Tova
Joseph Honigman, M.D.

Simhat Torah Honorees
Friday, September 30, 1983
Lewis Ansbacher
Hatan Torah
Charles Mizrahi
Hatan Bereshit
Blanche Slott
Woman of Valor
This year Lewis Ansbacher
received the honor of “Hatan
Torah” (Bridegroom of the
Torah). His diligent and tireless
efforts on behalf of the Center’s
Education, Transportation,
House and Campsite committees,
over the past 25 years, have
earned him this distinguished
honor. Over the years, “Lukie”
has maintained an abiding interest
in the Center, working for the
most part, behind the scenes, to
strengthen the Center’s programs
and financial base.
As a respected member of the
Board of Trustees and the
Executive committee, he is often
sought after for his advice “When
Lukie Talks Everyone Listens.”
The community has also
benefitted from his brilliant legal
mind as well. He was president of
the J.F.C.S. and the Duval
County Legal Aid Society. When
ever called upon he is quick to
respond to the needs of the
congregation... and because of
this dedication we honor Lewis
Ansbacher as our Hatan Torah.
Our “Hatan Bereshit,”
Charles Mizrahi, was chosen
“Bridegroom of the Beginning,” a
very fitting honor as he has been
a man of many beginnings.
At 37, he was one of the
youngest presidents of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center-a
young man with many visions. It
was during his administration
that the young couples’ club,
Ha’Rayim, was formed and the
Center Car Raffle was initiated.
Charles was responsible for
coordinating Building Fund rallies
which preceded our move from
Third and Silver - the highlight of
his presidency and another new
beginning.
The Center is indebted to him
for the part he played in
supporting Jewish Education and
the Center’s youth program. His
children have been officers of
their youth groups demon¬
strating the same leadership
qualities as their father.
A third generation Mizrahi,
Charles comes from a lineage of
dedicated and philanthropic
people. His melodious voice and
Torah reading have become
favorites of many Shabbat
worshippers. This is a man who
truly deserves our admiration.
Blanche Slott was chosen
“Woman of Valor” for her
devotion and sensitivity to the
needs of the youth of the Center.
The distinguished leadership she
provided the Sisterhood during
her three year term as president,
is also reflected by her service to
scouting and other youth
activities.
She is credited for organizing 3
Girl Scout troops and 5 Brownie
troops and served as a leader as
well.
Recognizing her dedication,
she was elected to serve on the
Center board as Youth
Commission chairman, which
gave her the distinction of being
the first woman board member.
A hard worker and talented
artist, Blanche is always willing to
share her creativity. Presently,
Blanche is serving as Administra¬
tive Director and brings to her
job the knowledge and
experience she has acquired
through her years as a volunteer.
Our Woman of Valor is
extremely worthy of the honor.
We congratulate the families of
our honorees.
Daily Minyan
Minyan captains, Barney Margolin and
Jack Silverman are calling for Minyan
while Sid Berkowitz suggests names.
The Jacksonville Jewish Center takes
pride in its Daily Minyan. More than 100
different men are involved in this mitzvah.
Through the tireless efforts of the captains
and co-captains, we have minyans every
morning and evening.
The Daily Minyan needs you. For a
satisfying and rewarding experience attend
once or twice a month on a regular basis.
Weekday evenings are in need of men to
make a minyan, please make an effort to
attend whenever possible.
We attribute our success to the following
minyan captains:
SUNDAY Philip Selber, a.m.;
Nathan Shmunes & Bill Goldberg, p.m.
MONDAY .. .Dr. Nathan Schneider, a.m.;
Sy Freedman, p.m.
TUESDAY Blanche Slott, a.m.;
Martin Brauner & Dr. Michael Greenburg,
p.m.
WEDNESDAY Harry Berman, a.m.;
Jack Silverman & Barney Margolin, p.m.
THURSDAY Norman Moss, a.m.;
Barney Margolin, p.m.
FRIDAY Sonny Sandler, a.m.

A Year of
We now praise good and generous men and women who have come before us, as well as those in our midst who labor
on behalf of the House of God.
Setzer Social Hall
October 15, 1983
The Center’s “Year of Dedication” was initiated with the official naming of the
Setzer Social Hall.
The Setzer Social Hall is named for Benjamin Setzer, of blessed memory, and
memorializes his leadership and generosity. His willingness in offering the initial
gifts; his maintenance of a continuous flow of substantial financial contributions
over a period of more than 25 years; and above all, his counsel and determination
have made it possible for the synagogue, to have had available in the 50s and 60s,
the building facilities so desperately needed then for the religious education of the
increasing number of congregants and children.
Benjamin Setzer also encouraged the acquisition of the property on State Road
13 and his enthusiasm helped concretize the final plans for the development of
our present facility.
The Setzer Social Hall dedication is not only a congregation’s collective
remembrance of an heroic personality of the past as it is also our
acknowledgment of the gratitude we feel for the nurturing of a family legacy of
generosity today.
Benjamin Setzer
The family of Benjamin Setzer has
continued his legacy. They are in the
forefront of the Center leadership as it
plans for the future development of the
physical facilities.
L-R, Bessie Frisch, Hannah Setzer,
Leonard Setzer, Leah Levit.
With every Brit and naming of a child, every Bar and
Bat Mitzvah reception, every Confirmation, every
wedding celebrated in the Setzer Social Hall. .. with
every meeting, gathering, class and lecture held
withing those walls and graced by Setzer Garden,
Ben Setzer’s immortality is assured.

===== PAGE 40 =====
Dedication
Witten Chapel
December 2, 1983
The Witten Chapel is in the “hub of the daily life of the
congregation.” Morning and afternoon services as well as early
Shabbat services on Friday evening, are held there. Its warm and
intimate atmosphere make it a perfect place for the minyan, Torah
Study classes, daily services for the Solomon Schechter Day
School, and the Junior Congregation services which are held on
Shabbat and holidays. Since it can be expanded to seat 100 people,
smaller weddings and the Friday evening services of the Bar and
Bat Mitzvah are held there.
To memorialize the love and respect for their
parents and grandparents, the families of Dr.
Joseph, Ike, Dr. Samuel and the late Louis
Witten dedicated the Witten Chapel in memory
of Ida and Max Witten.
Sisterhood Kitchen Dedication
January 28, 1984
A Pledge of Allegiance — During the Sisterhood administration of Susan Kantor, a $100,000 pledge was made to the
Center’s Building Fund to be used toward the furnishing of the comprehensive kitchen facility. Monies were to be raised
annually by a “Donor Affair,” each time counting on the generosity of the Sisterhood membership, and every year our ladies
came through because of careful planning and solicitations made by the donor chairwomen. As a result of the time, effort and
success of their leadership, %’s of the pledge has been paid.
The Donor Chairwomen Honored Were: Isabel Balotin, Barbara Cantor, Ellen Freedman, Maxine Funk, Marilyn
Garber, Rhoda Goldstein, Renee Gordon, Joan Levin, Helaine Marón, Ginette Mizrahi, Evelyn Moskovitz, Rhonda Passink,
Lois Peltz, Sue Rosenberg, Barbara Safer, Merle Selevan, Debra Setzer and Joni Shmunes.
The highlight of the day was the dedication of the Kitchen. The Center, Building Fund Committee, the Youth and Education
departments all praise the good works of the Sisterhood.

SHALOM:
Before we begin a New Year of “generating
positives” let us stop to thank those wonderful
women upon whose accomplishments we will
build. Sisterhood donors enabled us to
dedicate the synagogue kitchen in their honor.
Card Party participants purchased new tables
for all of us to use. Torah Fund contributors
help the Jewish Theological Seminary Library
and Mathilde Schechter Residence Hall. Art
Auction proceeds help support our many
Youth activities and holiday celebrations.
Besides filling our bodies with delicious food; our minds with
music; stimulating programs; and book reviews; we enrich our
souls with D’vrai Torah, Sisterhood Shabbat and a Rosh Chodesh
service.
New members, old members, Soviet Jewry, Social Action,
hospital visits. . .our Chai Lites keeps us informed about what’s
happening as well as what the busy fund raising ladies have
available. Not only does our lovely Gift Shop bring in needed
revenue, it enriches our homes and lives with Judaica.
We have a 59 year history of service to the Center and the
community. Wht about the coming year? Are you going to help
“generate positives?” Are you going to sit on the sidelines, feel like
an outsider, or will you join in making Sisterhood a warm place
where all are welcome?
As we reach out and work together we will be a true
SISTERHOOD - a network of support - Jewish women doing
Jewish things and we will be positively blessed.
Joseph, my husband, the president, joins me in wishing that each
of you and your loved ones be inscribed for a good year.
Sisterhood Installation 1984

Sisterhood Bat Mitzvah Class

who want to engage in an intensive study of the prayerbook,
the Shabbat service, Jewish history, holidays and Jewish
philosophy and thought. The course extends over a two-year
period of time. -

The Solomon Schechter Day School P.T.A.
Sweet Smell of Success
.
mwmmmm
Mrs. Shirley Bielski, Past President of the Solomon Schechter Day
School PTA, is shown presenting an eight pound chocolate bar to the
Second Grade Class. The candy bar was first prize for selling $485.00
Barbara Safer worth of chocolate during the PTA sale.
Overall, the entire sale total for the school surpassed all goals. The
student body sold $2,240.00 worth of candy during a two week period
of sales. Of this amount, the PTA retains 50% for funding projects for
the Solomon Schechter students, PTA, and school during this event.
The Solomon Schechter PTA provides a connection between parents and the school administration and faculty. This
year our monthly meetings will be held on the third Thursday of each month.
In addition, profits realized from our fund-raising projects - such as: magazine sale, Book Fair, candy sale, will be used
to provide equipment and materials to enhance the program of the Solomon Schechter Day School. PTA also actively
serves the school: hot lunches, eye screening, art appreciation, holiday observances and library are a few of the ways.
As president of the P.T.A., I hope that all parents will join and assist in our efforts to improve the quality of the
education and communication among all involved.
Barbara Safer

Henry Kramer Library & Resource Center
One of the greatest treasures of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is the Henry
Kramer Library and Resource Center. The shelves are filled with new as well as
other timely books on a great variety of Jewish subjects for the entire Jewish Center
family. There is Fiction, Humor, Art, Music, Religion, Philosophy, Biographies,
Zionism, Reference, etc.
Truly the pleasant and lovely furnishings of the Library should encourage
everyone to drop by and enjoy a good book.
With the assistance of the PTA Mothers and Librarian Louis Cohen, the Solomon
Schechter Day School collection was available for the Day School students and the
Hebrew School students. This collection has numerous fine reference books and
many delightful fiction books with Judaica themes.
The Library and the Center Sisterhood presented two excellent Book Reviews for
the congregation. Teddie Moskovitz and Rose Entman reviewed two historical
novels by Brenda Segal.
The Library Cart is available at Kiddush on several Saturdays through the year. It
gives members opportunity to check out books and peruse the many fine magazines
and periodicals.
Library Committee members devote many service hours to maintain this facility.
It would be impossible to function without their assistance.
The Library is grateful for the generous support of the Center membership.
Member contributions are used to purchase new books and library supplies.
Come by and enjoy the attractive Reading Room. You will find “Moment,”
“Commentary,” “Near East Report,” “Ba’Lam,” Jerusalem Week, Jerusalem Post,
Jewish Post and Opinion, Yiddish Newspapers and many other magazines and
periodicals.

Adult Education
Hebrew Literacy
The Hebrew Literacy Campaign has one major goal ... to make
every adult a literate Jew by teaching each one how to read from a
Siddur; and making them comfortable in the synagogue. Beginner
and intermediate classes are held during the day and evening.
Classes & Activities
Israeli Folk Dancing - Latest dances from Israel are taught
Haftorah and Torah Skills - Musical skill of reading Torah trope
and notes are taught
Book Reviews - Current books and periodicals are reviewed
Torah Study Sessions - Weekly discussions of the “portion of the
week”
Minyanaire Program - Sunday morning breakfast and discussions
Once in a New Moon - Lunch and learn program
Scholar-in-Residence - Outstanding scholars and thinkers share
their knowledge
Film Festival - Light and entertaining films for the whole family
Visiting Scholars and Lecturers
The hosting Havurah, Ananchnu-
Mispacha, enjoys a light moment
with Rabbi Emil Fackenheim.
Dr. Neil Gillman, associate
provost of the Jewish Theological
Seminary, was a guest scholar in
March.
Danny Siegel, author and lecturer,
visited the Solomon Schechter
Day School and explained the
importance of Tzedakah.
Internationally acclaimed expert in
Jewish medical ethics, Dr. Fred
Rosner, discussed very
controversial topics during his
visit.
Substance of a Havurah
good friends . . . meaningful activities . . . fantastic food
Havurah members engage in a range of activities from holiday celebrations, to serious study, to just plain fun. They furthermore
engage in creating indepth friendships and mutual support. Groups generally average 10-20 adults and their families. They meet on a
regular basis in homes and in synagogues.
This year the Havurah, Ananchnu-Mispacha presented a dramatic slide presentation of a mock trial of Anatoly Shcharansky for the
Jacksonville Jewish Community.

Cemetery Committee of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center
Michael Schneider Kenneth Bowden
The Cemetery Committee provides a very necessary function of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. It is very
important that the Cemetery grounds are well kept and provide a peaceful resting place for our loved ones.
Our Cemetery Committee is chaired by Michael Schneider. Serving on the committee are Hymie Selber, Alan
Taffet, Dr. Joe Witten, Dr. Sam Witten, Jack Bettman, Joel Bressler, Nathan Sandler, Jack Becker and Joe
Becker.
Mr. Kenneth A. Bowden, Controller of the Jacksonville Jewish Center, also serves as general manager of our
Cemetery. It is his responsibility to oversee the upkeep and maintenance of the grounds. He has an excellent
working relationship with Mr. Jennewine who is general manager of Evergreen Cemetery. Mr. Jennewine has been
very generous with his time and his staff, Mr. Campbell, Mr. Miller and Mrs. Phillips. They have all taken excellent
care of the Center’s property, above and beyond what is expected. We appreciate everything they do.
Johnnie B. Mercer, who has been custodian of the cemeteries for 25 years, is in virtual retirement. Maintenance
is now handled by Russell and Winifred Baker, a very dependable couple. We are very appreciative of the help
given us by John Bergeron of the Southern Monument Company.

Seated: Joel Bressler, Bea Browdy
STEPS WHICH SHOULD BE TAKEN TO FACILITATE SIMPLE JEWISH BURIAL ACCORDING TO THE CUSTOM
OF OUR COMMUNITY:
Upon a Jewish persons death an undertaker is called to move the body to the preparation room of the funeral home
where the features are set, bodily excretions are briefly washed off and the orifices are packed. The body is then wrapped in
a cloth sheet. A Hevrah Kaddisha committee (the Holy Society whose members have been trained to prepare a body for
burial) is called to the funeral home to wash the body which rests on a special wooden board, according to prescribed ritual.
While performing this work the committee recites certain prayers which befit the occasion. After the committee washes the
body, the members dress the body in white linen shrouds and place it in a plain, simple, wooden casket which is unadorned
except for a wooden Star of David which is attached to the top.
If the burial takes place on the same day that death has occurred, the body is transported to the cemetery for the funeral
services. If the funeral takes place on the following day (or later, if out-of-town relatives will attend), a “shomer” (watchman)
called by the Hevra Kaddisha sits with the body during the night; the body must never be left unattended. If it is desired to
have the funeral service in a chapel prior to interment, the chapel must be non-sectarian; that is, no Christian symbols may
be visible during the service.
The following persons must be called by the family or the undertaker as soon as possible after death has ocurred: the
rabbi, the Hevra Kaddisha, the person in charge of the Jewish cemetery, the burial vault company and the cemetery
association which contacts the grave-diggers.
In the event that death occurs in another locality, the out-of-town undertaker may arrange with either of two local funeral
homes, Hardage & Son-Estes Krauss or George Hewell & Sons, to use its facilities for the participation of the Hevra
Kaddisha and the shomer when applicable. These establishments will also indicate how to contact the above persons.
Finally, it is to be clearly understood that no embalming or cremation or public viewing of the body in an open casket is to
take place. If interment must be postponed beyond twenty-four hours, the body may be kept in a body cooler to retard
decomposition.

FOR IMMEDIATE RELEASE
JACKSONVILLE LINKED TO PALM BEACH
For the first time in Jacksonville there will now be a direct line to the Israel Bond Office in Palm
Beach. This new line will link the people of Jacksonville with the office in Palm Beach to
facilitate greater service to the dedicated leaders in the Jacksonville Israel Bond Organization.
The great advantage will be to answer all questions directly concerning Bond transfers,
redemption and discrepancies in accounts. For campaign problems Bond buyers will be able
to speak with Bert Sales, Florida State Director or Allan Kreitman, his associate.
The new phone number is 356-3012 and the caller will be connected directly with the Palm
Beach Office.
Another step in furthering of service to Jacksonville will be via the Jewish Federation and
local synagogues. They will now have a supply of Israel Bond applications and return
envelopes so that anyone in Jacksonville may purchase an Israel Bond when there is no active
Israel Bond campaign going on at the time.
National Israel Bonds has recognized the leadership role Jacksonville has had in the sale of
Israel Bonds. They feel this new link between the cities of Jacksonville and Palm Beach will
lead to further growth of the Jacksonville Israel Bond Campaign.
Buy Israel Bonds for the Future of your children and Israel’s children.

When man departs from this world,
Neither silver nor gold nor precious
stones accompany him;

But a good name endures forever.
Happy is the man who has acquired a good name,
And retains it when he departs this world.

St. Vincent’s Family Medical Care Centers are staffed by a full¬
time physician. We operate seven days a week, 365 days a year,
from 9 a.m. to 10 p.m. After hours, St. Vincent’s offers on-call
physicians telephone coverage for established patients. Walk
right in or call for an appointment and see how quickly and ef¬
ficiently we take care of you.
St. Vincent’s Family Medical Care Centers are modem, profes¬
sionally staffed and fully equipped health care centers. On-site X-
rays, lab procedures and tests are available as needed.
You will be pleasantly surprised to find that our services cost
significantly less than comparable treatment at a hospital
emergency room. Our goal is to bring competent medical care to
your family conveniently and economically.
St. Vincent’s Family Medical Care Centers are now in five neigh¬
borhoods, and soon to be in three more. Centers are open at
Regency Square, Ponte Vedra, Glynlea, Lakewood and Orange
Park. In 1984, centers will be open in Downtown, Baymeadows
and the Roosevelt Mall area. You’re invited to stop in anytime to
visit. We’ll be happy to show you our modem facilities and ex¬
plain the Family Medical Care concept.

Early Childhood Department
Young children enter Pre-school at difficult stages of
development and with various backgrounds of experience.
Most children have short attention spans and high energy
levels. Opportunities are provided for them to learn through
active involvement and an abundance of multi-leveled activities.
Children need to feel successful and important. They must establish positive attitudes about
themselves. We have, in Jacksonville Jewish Center Early Childhood Department at all levels,
developed a program and curriculum that will give children the experiences that will help them
develop healthy self-concepts and form the foundation for future learning.
Our Day Care has been created to provide a secure, stimulating and safe place for all Jewish
children in the community, to learn as they play. We are very proud of the Day Care program we
have created and know it is the quality child care program where parents and children can find a
secure loving atmosphere.
— Marilyn Sandler
Administrator
Solomon Schechter Day School
At the Solomon Schechter we are blessed with many sources
of vigor. Our strength lies in talented and caring teachers
whose skills and devotion combine to provide their students
with the most enriching and individualized elementan;
education possible.
We are ever expanding and improving our curriculum to insure that our students receive an
outstanding secular education integrated with Judaic studies and principles. Increasingly, faculty
members have developed units of integrated study that bridge the Judaic and Secular worlds.
Our language arts and math programs have continued to be expanded and clarified to provide
clear scope and sequence to enable us to monitor students’ progress.
These movements forward are not isolated events, but represent the combined efforts of
many. Among those who contribute are our parents, who through their PTA organization,
support our profesisonal and lay leadership. The lay leadership, through its Education
Committee, and the religious leadership, with its support staff headed by Rabbi Gaffney,
continue to exhibit loyal, dedicated support of the school and its purposes.
Strengthened by these contributions and our commitment to constantly reassess, improve
and surpass our previous achievements, we will keep our school a stronghold for the acquisition
of knowledge.
— Willard Kennedy
Principal
Willard Kennedy
Marilyn Sandler

Solomon Schechtcr Day School
“Jewish and American heritage blended into one world”
The Campus is located in the school wing of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. The Day School has
the unlimited use of a library, computer room, gym, sports field, stage, swimming pool, tennis courts,
and chapel.

Curriculum
JUDAIC . . A full program of Judaic-Hebraic learning
experiences are integrated into the daily schedule.
Students gain significant insights into the teachings of
Judaism and develop appreciation of the ideas and
values expressed in Jewish literature, music and art.
SECULAR . . . The child is the center of the
educational process, therefore our programs are
designed to provide maximum growth of each
individual. Emphasis is on the mastery of basic
language, mathematical skills and the development of
concepts in science and social studies.

SUNDAY SCHOOL
The Sunday School of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is planned expressly for children in Kindergarten, First
and Second Grades. A two hour program gives each child the opportunity to experience the richness of
his/her Jewish heritage through song, dance, role playing, cooking, short stories, games, arts and crafts.
Emphasis is placed on the holidays and festivals; Jewish values and mitzvot are encouraged.

The Afternoon Hebrew School of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is designed for students in grades 3-7 and provides
an elementary education leading to Bar/Bat Mitzvah and continuation in the high school program.
Meeting twice during the week and on Saturdays, “the basics” are at the core of the curriculum, with stress on
Hebrew reading, Jewish Social Studies, and current events relating to Israel. Synagogue skills, holiday observances and
knowledge of prayers are all part of the comprehensive Afternoon Hebrew School program.

Hebrew High School
The Judaica High School is the creation of the synagogue to offer Jewish youth an opportunity to explore the broad
expanse of resources available through our heritage. This program seeks to provide exciting, innovative exploration of
Judaism upon which each student might build. It involves children in 8th through 11th grades and is required for
Confirmation.

The Jacksonville Jewish Center’s Recreation Program provides N. y
good wholesome fun for both our members and for the entire n. "
Jewish community. From the annual Alexander Brest Tennis Tournament in \
October through Day Camp which begins in June, the Center provides
activities for all ages. Cub, Boy and Girl Scout Troops are sponsored by
the Center, Sunday Sports Association Basketball is the only sports program
in Jacksonville which caters to Jewish youth, and our facilities are unmatched
anywhere. An Olympic sized pool, surrounded by woods, tennis courts, ball fields
playground, all provide unlimited recreation for your family.
Summer activities included our expanded Family Program, which features EXCLUSIVE
use of our beautiful nine acre campsite facility and pool seven days per week. Our eight
week summer Day Camp has programs for children age 2 thru grade 9. For more information
and rates, please call the Center.

Center Day Camp
Day Camping can be one of the most meaningful experiences a child will ever have. Our camp offers not
only a situation in which children can learn and develop by interacting with other children, but it offers a full
scope of organized activities designed to make a child aware of our Jewish heritage; to develop new
friendships; enjoy the wonders of nature that may be found on our large wooded campsite; and the
importance of active sports.
This year the Center summer camp programs offered a full- or half-day program for campers ages 2-8; and
our specialty camps included a fine arts and computer camp for older campers.

Torah Readers
We at the Jacksonville Jewish Center consider ourselves indeed fortunate to possess the kind of human resources that we have;
and nowhere is this more true than in the area of Torah Readers.
During the year, our congregants had the pleasure of listening to 62 skilled and fluent Ba’aley K’riah (Torah Readers). Some are
recent B’nai Mitzvah; others are young men who are graduates from the religious schools of the Center and were trained by Ted
Gross. Some are transplants from other communities who have read Torah using their own special Torah trope notes.
Each man, young and old, volunteered his time to enhance our Shabbat and holiday services. We are grateful to them and express
our sincere YASHER KOACH!
The following men served as Torah Captains this past year:

Ted Gross Retires
After thirty years of dedicated service to the congregation, Ted Gross retired. A special dinner was held in his honor on
October 6, 1983, headed by Jeffery Morris and Jack Shorstein. Many of his former students and friends expressed their
warm wishes of appreciation and shared their humorous and meaningful experiences.
Ted served as Director of Education for twenty-seven years and is responsible for teaching Torah and Torah trope to
many of the men who are now reading from the Torah. The knowledge and influence he has had on the youth of this
congregation will be everlasting.
The pictures featured on this page were taken at the Tribute Dinner for Ted Gross.

CAMP RAMAH
Adds a New Dimension
to Your Child's Growth as a Jew
RAMAH??? WHAT S A RAMAH???
RAMAH is a talk with a friend or a counselor who really does
understand . . .
RAMAH is living in a bunk with 13 other great kids.
RAMAH is participating in a Hebrew play and knowing what you’re
saying.
RAMAH is Havdalah by the lake after the sun has set.
RAMAH is learning to care for animals.
RAMAH is carpentry projects in Arts and Crafts.
RAMAH is an overnight.
RAMAH is choosing your own activity — and being trusted to live
by your choice.
RAMAH is getting called out in baseball on strikes — in HEBREW.
RAMAH is singing in a camp-wide Song Festival with 400 other
kids.
RAMAH is that wonderful Shabbat meal.
RAMAH is knowing that there are people who care.
RAMAH is participating in a talent show for your division.
RAMAH IS MORE ....
RAMAH is your child — this summer — if you want it to be.
Front row - L-R Laura Greenburg, Beth
Greenburg, Cheryl Bossen, Steven
Shapiro, Simeon Abramson.
Back row - L-R Judith Jacobson,
Manya Lazarus
Camp Ramah provides the opportunity of a total Jewish living experience for children and teenagers in the
relaxed atmosphere of a summer camp. Values built on a shared experience and emotion reach our sons and
daughters in a manner impossible in a formal school program. Over the years, RAMAH has helped instill a deeper
commitment to Judaism in many of its participants.
The Center believes that benefits accrue to the congregation, not just to the individual. We have therefore made
monies available to reduce the financial cost of qualified students regardless of need. These monies are not part of
the regular Center budget, but rather are raised by donations to the Myra Thier Lazarus Ramah Fund, and
Sisterhood, and from other sources.
Two families have helped us greatly. The Gordon Family has established a scholarship fund in memory of the
beloved Robert J. Gordon. A long list of deserving boys and girls have been able to go to Ramah because of this
scholarship. Abe Selber established in his will a perpetual trust for specific Jewish education purposes. With the full
support of his children, Iris and Franklin, who have never lost interest in the Center, the proceeds of the Abe
Selber Trust have been used to send campers to Ramah.
Our appreciation to Horty Gendzier, who has worked so diligently to coordinate this very worthwhile
program.
Ramah in Israel Seminar participant — Stephanie Katz.

White Water Rafting
Wonderful! Terrific! Fantastic!
There are no other words to
describe the five day Kadima
Camping Trip to North
Carolina. A group consisting of
ten - thirteen year olds, and
four inexperienced adults were
led by Rabbi Kentof into the
wilds of North Carolina. This
ambitious dream turned into a
reality due to the love and
devotion that Rabbi Kentof has
for the youth of our
congregation.
While in North Carolina
many of us experienced times
that we never had before —
from services under the stars,
cooking over an open fire,
sleeping in tents, and rafting
down white water rapids.
The real challenge of this trip
was how such a close group
could remain close without
bathing for five days. However,
everyone worked together and
depended on one another to
make this one of the most
memorable trips of our lives.
As a member of the Board,
and as Youth Commission
Chairman, but most of all as a
parent, I would like to express
my thanks to Rabbi Kentof for
making such a trip possible.
Our congregation is very
fortunate to have a man of this
calibre leading our youth
programs. The benefits of
these experiences will be
everlasting.
I would like to personally
thank the entire group for
giving me the opportunity to
attend; and for bringing me
back alive!
Sincerely,
Robert Cantor

Message from the Youth and Education Director
Rabbi Dov Kentof
You and I have been sending our children to Jewish schools. We have
invested in their Jewish education our own money, community funds, the
children’s precious time and efforts. Has it all been worthwhile? Have the
returns justified the investments?
But what returns should we expect? How can we measure and evaluate
them? Educational returns are so intangible.
Indeed they are, but not as intangible as we may think. We should and we do
have some ways of measuring them.
It is of course very simple to measure objectively the achievements of our children in terms of subject
matter, such as Bible, Hebrew, History, etc. We do possess the technical equipment and devices of
measuring accurately what our child has learned at any given time in any of the school subjects.
But, you may argue, knowledge is not enough; it is attitudes that count; it is the cultivation of character, of
the religious personality, and the like, that is significant.
Quite true. We all realize that mere cold-blooded knowledge is not enough. Knowledge has no value unless
it glows with the impulse to action. Knowledge must be dynamic, it must serve both as a motor and as a
rudder. It should galvanize its possessor into action; it should also guide and direct such action.
We, here, at the Jacksonville Jewish Center are committed to provide your child with the skills and the
attitude for Jewish life. Through the many programs that we offer to your child, we strengthen your child’s
commitment to Judaism and to the synagogue. We do hope that you will take advantage of our multi-program
and that this year will bring fulfillment, understanding and commitment to all of you!
Alina, Gil and Tali are joining me in extending to you and your family a happy New Year.
Rabbi Dov Kentof
Rabbi Dov Kentof
f/
“Love” “Adventure” “Friendship”

CHALUTZIM
Grades 5 and 6
General Aim: Jewish families today look to the synagogue as the center for Jewish activity: religious,
education, social and recreational. A major goal of the synagogue and its school is the education of youth with
a firm base of knowledge, Jewish identification of youth, a sense of pride in their heritage, and a commitment
to Judaism. The goal of Chalutzim is to bring about the internalization of Jewish values, attitudes and
behavior patterns by supplementing the child’s formal religious education with informal Jewish learning
experience.
Call the Youth Office for more information, 268-6736, ext. 435.
Members of Chalutzim were actively involved in the Kadima Convention and had a year full of exciting activities.

United Synagogue Youth
U.S.Y. — Grades 9-12
Officers — 1984-85
President

The general aim of the United Synagogue Youth program is to bring about a meaningful and fully reciprocal
encounter of Judaism, the Jewish people, and the synagogue on one side, and the Jewish teenager on the
other. As a result of this encounter, the Jewish teenager will, firstly, demonstrate and experience how the
Jewish way of living, through study, action and fellowship leads the way to personal fulfillment and growth
while meeting his spiritual and social needs; and secondly, make a significant contribution to his synagogue,
community, society and the Jewish people.

Seventh Annual Kadima Convention
The Jacksonville Jewish Center hosted its largest convention ever! Thirty chapters from our Southeast Region sent their delegates
to Jacksonville to participate.
The overall theme — “To Repair the Universe” — dealt with subjects of hunger in the world and the Jewish approach toward the
poor, nuclear disarmament, and the relationship between man and his fellow man.
Our delegates conducted services, arranged a special Havdalah Service and created the entire program for the weekend. On
Saturday night, a social and carnival were held for young people to enjoy.
This was by far the largest convention of its kind in the country and was regarded as the focal point of Kadima activities in the
Southeast Region. Our regional director, Mr. Bruce Klasner, addressed the young people during the convention. Activities were
directed by our convention coordinators Beth Greenburg, Jenny Verstandig, Katherine Echt, David Silverman; supervised by
advisors Fran Manas, Kim Lewis and Rabbi Dov Kentof.
Our thanks to all the families of the Center who graciously hosted our guests.
Best Wishes
Flowers Baking Co.

Cub Scouts Pack 14
Cub Scouts is the phase of Boy Scouts that
includes boys 8, 9 & 10 years of age. The purpose of
this program is to develop good character and
encourage spiritual growth, good citizenship, good
sportsmanship, comraderie with other boys, and a
sense of personal achievement.
Pack 14 had four very successful and rewarding
dens who met weekly under the guidance of
volunteer leaders. Once a month the whole pack
and their families met for such activities as:
Pinewood Derby, Scout Sabbath, Blue and Gold
Banquet, a campout and guest speakers. At these
meetings the boys shared their den
accomplishments, put on skits, and were
ceremoniously given badges they earned.
The success of Cub Scouts depends on adult
support and involvement. Please call if you can help.
A very special thank you to Lanny Zimmerman for
all his help, guidance and understanding.
Happy Scouting,
Carole Goldberg

Brownies and Girl Scouts
For many years, the Center Sisterhood has actively sponsored the Brownie and Girl Scout
Troops of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. Scouting is a very important phase of the youth
program in the Center. It helps develop character, usefulness at home, appreciation of nature
and the out-of-doors, creation of objects of beauty and usefulness from simple things, and it
helps these young people to find their places in the synagogue and community through
service.
Under the able guidance of Mrs. Clara Mann, the entire Brownie and Girl Scout program
provides all of these opportunities for our young women of tomorrow. For further
information, please call Mrs. Mann.
LTI — A Wonderful Experience
About 40 young people from the Jacksonville Jewish Center Youth Department spent one week at LTI in the
mountains of North Carolina - studying, singing, interacting, and making new friends.
The USY overall theme, “Jerusalem,” was enhanced by a dramatic presentation, evening programs, and many
other exciting events. The Kadima overall theme was “The Many Faces of Judaism,” which dealt with the various
streams of Jewish life.
The young people participated in a mass game of experience/discussion groups; they met with Rabbis and
educators; and had many experiences in leadership development.
All of the young people are looking forward to another year of exciting programs.

Boy Scout Troop 14

* New members
Scoutmaster: Randy Silverberg
Assistant Scoutmasters: Bill Wilensky, Stephen Davis,
Dan Wilensky
Committee Chairman: Steve Ghelerter
Committee Member: Ira Jackler
The sky is the limit for the scouts of Troop 14. The Troop was founded in 1919 by Rabbi S. Stein. Sixty-five years later, Troop 14 is going
strong. The busy agenda of outdoor activities, camping and exciting programs continued in 1983-84 as scouting rides a wave of renewed
popularity.
The Troop began the year with a visit to the University of Florida. The scouts lodged at the Hillel Foundation, joining the collegiates for
Shabbat services. The Troop watched the “Fighting Gator” football team trounce its opponent. The scouts occupied Florida Field for a
game of their own. The boys visited the incredible Florida State Museum while in the university city.
The outdoor camping agenda began with a weekend at St. Augustine’s Anastasia State Park. The Troop hiked through the historic city
and visited the interesting sites and historical landmarks, leaving a trace of history of their own.
Winter saw Troop 14 return to Boy Scout Camp Echockatee, a favorite camping area over the years. Troop 14 owned and maintained a
large cabin at the site for earlier generations of Scouts. The camp was the location for last year’s successful First Annual Old-Timer’s
Campout and Reception.
Troop 14 inaugurated the Osceola National Forest as its newest camping location in February. The Troop included the spectacular re¬
enactment of the Civil War Battle of Olustee in its weekend events. The scouts reveled in the nostalgic event and joined the festive activities
commemorating the infamous battle.
Fort Clinch State Park hosted Troop 14 during the weekend of the Fernandina Arts Festival. The scouts explored the unique Civil War
era fort and enjoyed the Park’s beach and fishing pier. The weekend was highlighted by a jaunt to the nearby art extravaganza.
Among the many other activities this past year, the Troop enjoyed a campfire visit from the Baptist Hospital Life Flight helicopter, the
annual Blue and Gold Banquet and a Jacksonville Bulls’ football game.
Jeffrey Ghelerter, Michael Weitzen, Adam DePaul, Sean Usoff, Roger Golcher, Ray Whaley and Jamey McClure attended summer scout
camp at Camp Shands in Melrose. The scouts returned from camp with an even greater enthusiasm for scouting and nearly 30 merit badges
of which to boast.
Boy Scout Troop 14 is an organization for boys grades 6 to 12. The Troop fosters the scouting ideals of friendship, citizenship, reverence,
personal growth and self reliance in a program designed to tantalize the diversified interests of today’s youth.
The Center “Keeps in Touch” With College Students
Because we care about our college age youth, the Center maintains an on-going program to
“keep in touch.” Not only do we send the Bulletin, but we also try to bring the holidays a little
closer by sending a variety of holiday packages throughout the year; current events relating to
Israel and the Jewish community also get sent.
Rabbis Gaffney and Kentof frequently visit nearby colleges and meet informally with
students.
This very important project is coordinated by Horty Gendzier. If you have a college age child,
please send his/her address to the Center office.
Herb Lewitt and daughter
Melanie after her graduation.

Neal F. Portnoy Youth Lounge
The Neal F. Portnoy Youth Lounge was made possible
through the generosity of the Louis Portnoy family. This well-
equipped and well-designed facility is used to serve the needs
of the youth of our congregation and the Jewish youth of the
entire community. It is the central location for formal
meetings, programs and activities. It also serves as a
synagogue for youth services.
Equipped with all sorts of games, such as pinball machines,
foozball, bumper pool, electronic and board games, the youth
lounge has something for everyone.

contributed clothing and a variety of good saleable
items.

The Jacksonville Jewish Community Council was founded in
1935 and became the Jacksonville Jewish Federation in 1979. We
are almost 50 years old and are continuing to serve the Jewish
community in a variety of ways.
On June 5, 1983, we moved into our new home at 10829 Old St.
Augustine Rd. We have been able to make our meeting rooms
available to the different Jewish organizations and to hold
community-wide functions.
This past year the Federation has sponsored various community
programs. In December we hosted the Israeli Chassidic Festival,
which was held downtown at the Civic Auditorium. On May 2nd we
co-sponsored, with the synagogues, Yom Hashoah — a beautiful
and meaningful Holocaust Remembrance Program. In January, the
Womens Division held Education Day, which is a program to
educate the community and is put together by the presidents of the
various women’s organizations.
In order to bring the Jewish community closer together, the
Federation publishes The Commentator, our monthly newspaper.
We have been able to expand local coverage and also add national
and international articles of Jewish interest.
We will continue to conduct the Annual Combined Jewish
Appeal, which raises monies for the United Jewish Appeal, as well
as other national agencies. Our local beneficiaries are River
Garden, Jewish Family and Community Services and the
Community Kosher Nutrition Program.
As we continue to grow and enter our 50th year, we invite
everyone to visit our new building and participate in all community
events.

Jewish Family and Community

JEWISH FAMILY AND COMMUNITY SERVICES SERVES PEOPLE JUST LIKE YOU!
Over the course of the past year, we’ve undergone a number of changes.
First, by now you’ve noticed that we changed our name and logo. Second, our long time executive director
retired. Most important of all, we’ve added, expanded and reassessed our services to the community.
Special new programs were instituted such as: developmental activities by our social worker with YOUR
pre-schoolers, a college assistance program (CAPS) to help get YOUR children through choosing and paying
for college, adoption information and referral packets, home health care packets, enhanced Jewish Family
Life Education programs and more.
We still perform all our traditional services from counseling to short-term financial assistance and
everything in-between.
We’re growing every day and our main goal is to serve you.
Your agency stands ready to meet your needs.
L’Shona Tova Tikatevu

Hebrew Home for the Aged
The River Garden Home, situated on the banks of the St. Johns River,
surrounded by beautiful gardens, is a vital integral part of the Jacksonville Jewish
community. There are few communities fortunate enough to have a geriatric care
and rehabilitation center that has the capacity and resources to provide 100% of the
long term care and short term rehabilitation needs of the local Jewish population.
River Garden, therefore, is grateful for the involvement and continued financial
support of the community which enables it to offer all residents a consistently high
level of care regardless of their personal finances.
The staff of River Garden is called upon to deal with some of the most profoundly
difficult human care problems 24 hours a day, 365 days a year. Human problems
have no simple solutions, no perfect answers. River Garden is in the fore-front of developing decent humane responses to
these problems. In doing so, it has been singled out by the major government and voluntary accrediting agencies as a model
care facility.
Through individualized plans of care, the Home tries to strike a living balance between institutional requirements and
individual needs, in a residential setting supportive of Jewish identity. River Garden encourages the “wellness” of the
individual. This positive accent on living, with a variety of social, cultural and recreational programs helps create the special
climate and tone of River Garden. River Garden is itself a focal point of Jewish activity and Jewish identity. It helps maintain
the integrity of Jewish families and is a beautiful expression of Jewish social ethic.
L’SHONO TOVAH
Chairman,
Admissions Bd. Dr. Michael M. Greenburg

River Garden Auxiliary
The River Garden Auxiliary Inc., formerly the Ladies Hebrew
Sheltering Aid Society, is entering its 60th year of “Service With
A Heart.”
The Auxiliary continues in their tradition to assist and help the
River Garden Board to provide a Home for our Senior Citizens,
who are no longer able to live alone, a home where they can find
comfort, security, medical care and enjoyment, spiritual,
physical and emotional stimulation and pride in their own
accomplishments. All this combined gives the feeling and knowledge that “Someone Cares.”
The Auxiliary provides the extra budgetary needs of the Home, such as furnishings, redecorating, office and infirmary
equipment, and Hobby Shop materials. Funds are raised through our Annual Tombola, Donors, Social Printing, Fifth
Commandments Placque, Dues, and Life Membership.
The residents enjoy the special parties planned and given by the Auxiliary for Chanukah, Purim, Mother’s and Father’s
Day.
The Auxiliary sponsors the Red Cross Ladies in-house service and a Volunteer Program, and these ladies extend both their
hands and their hearts in service to our residents.
We welcome all of you to join us in this deeply human involvement.
We wish you and yours Peace, Health, and Happiness for a New Year.
President Mrs. Mitchell Peltz (Lois)

Mount Carmel Gardens
Mount Carmel Gardens Tenant Association
1984-85
OFFICERS

Cecil Tyner
During the past year our building has undergone many changes-all good. The outside has been sandblasted and painted; the lobby and hall have been
completely done over-from the wall paper, to the floor covering, to repainting the woodwork and doors-a new look for us all to enjoy.
Starting with the Board of Directors of Mount Carmel Gardens, and on down to our very popular Mr. Charles Caplan, our Administrator; Margaret
Lovito, our co-Administrator; our very capable maintenance crew, and our 24-hour group of workers at the desk-we have wonderful and continuous
supervisory maintenance and protection, — as well as immediate help for sudden sickness if we ever need it. A very comfortable feeling.
The new slate of officers and their assisting board of the Mount Carmel Tenants Association, took over their duties June 12th -- the beginning of the
1984-85 year. We are sure they will give us as active and fun-filled a season, as did last year’s officials. 1983 was a wonderful year, and we’re hoping for
another one just as enjoyable.
The Entertainers, under the direction of Dottie Levine, is active and functioning; the Carmel Chorale, with Jim Jerrard as instructor, is continuously
learning and performing; - and now we have added a square dance group, with Chuck Joyeusaz as caller and Cecil Tyner as his assistant - and they are
having a wonderful time at their weekly sessions.
The Kosher Nutrition Center is another plus to the advantages of Living in Mount Carmel. Delicious lunches are served, not only to our tenants, but to
many who don’t live here, but enjoy coming for the meals. All Senior Citizens are welcome to come share a nutritious and delicious meal with us, five days
a week.
Meeting here on a regular basis is Mount Carmel Chapter of the AARP #350, the Hannah Senesch group of Hadassah; Upjohns Clinic once a month;
and podiatrist Steven Merrit twice a month. The Mount Carmel Newsletter is distributed free once a month.
There are always parties - all we need is an excuse: monthly birthdays, holidays, Christmas-Hanakuh, New Years Eve, outside entertainment, and
anything else that might pop up. Never a dull moment.
To all senior citizens who enjoy Bingo, come join us every Monday evening. Everyone is welcome to come and have fun with us. That also goes for the
singing group - if you like to sing, join us on Tuesday evenings. You’ll love it.
In fact, you’ll love everything about living in Mount Carmel - as we do.

Zionist Organization of America
Jacksonville District
Dr. Milton B. Mann, M.D.
The Zionist Organization of America has had another
successful year; and as has been our custom for over thirty
years, we have held an annual Jewish National Fund function to
plant a grove of one thousand trees in Israel. However, in three
out of the last four years we have succeeded in planting two
groves. This years’ honorees were Max and Rose Hochman. In
addition, we co-sponsored the Maccabiah program with Beth
Shalom. This year, our most important function, however, is
our support of our national organization which has been very
effective through the years and important in mobilizing support
for Israel in our government.
President
Dr. Milton B. Mann

Hadassah
Hadassah, the Women’s Zionist Organization of America, consists of over 370,000 dedicated members who work
patiently and vigorously towards bold achievements rooted in idealism and ideology.
The impact of Hadassah on contemporary Israel is felt in every corner of the land. Hadassah’s varied and broad
programs affects the lives and hopes of Israel’s citizens. Hadassah is the second largest employer in Israel.
In America, the women of Hadassah are dedicated to the furtherance of the democratic ideals of the United States. Our
American-scene projects include American Affairs, Jewish Education, Zionist Affairs and Zionist Youth Activities.
Funds are raised to support the Haddassah University Medical Center at Kiryat Hadassah and Mt. Scopus in Jerusalem,
Youth Aliyah, Hadassah Israel Education Services, Jewish National Fund and Youth Activities.
The Jacksonville Chapter is a coordinating board which includes three groups: TIKVA, which meets during the daytime,
on the second Tuesday, September through May; HANNAH SENESCH, which meets on the second Wednesday evening;
and SHIR-LI which also meets on the second Wednesday evening.
A new Business and Professional Group is currently being organized.
We invite new residents and unaffiliated women to join and learn more about Hadassah. There is a group for everyone
and we welcome your call. Please call one of the presidents or a membership chairperson and introduce yourself.
We wish everyone a Shana Tova-a good year, a year of good health and much happiness.
Jacksonville Chapter Board

The National Council of Jewish Women is the nation’s oldest women’s volunteer organization. Since its
birth in 1893, NCJW has been characterized by a dedication to serving humanity and advancing the heritage
of Judaism.
Today more than 100,000 members organized into over 200 Sections and Branches nationwide, continue
a tradition of community action and advocacy, focusing their attention on the priority areas of AGING,
CHILDREN AND YOUTH, WOMEN’S ISSUES, JEWISH LIFE AND ISRAEL.
The Jacksonville Section is currently involved in projects that include an annual Mental Health Forum, the
Art Enrichment program in the elementary schools, Pre-school vision screening and programming for the
Nutrition Center at Mt. Carmel, a fall Tay-sachs screening and delivery of kosher meals on wheels. Also
planned is NCJW’s successful “ Self Development Series.”
Through a coordinated program of education, service, advocacy and social action, NCJW WORKS IN
THE Jewish and general communities locally, nationally, and internationally.
The major thrust of NCJW’s activities in Israel has been to aid in the development of Israel’s children, its
most precious resource.
NCJW seeks members of all ages and interests.
An Evening Branch has been organized for those women who prefer evening meetings.
For more information, please contact Section President Dottie Shlafer at 731-8397 or Branch President
Barbara Black at 731-9359.
Jewish War Veterans
Jewish War Veterans Post 199
The JWV is the oldest active veterans organization in the U.S., founded in 1896. The Jewish
War Veterans not only works for and helps all veterans, regardless of religion, race, or national
origin, but it is a militant and patriotic voice of American Jewry.
The JWV stands up against bigotry and anti-semitism, and against the threat of cults. The
JWV also actively helps the Vietnam veterans. Active in community relations and community
service, within and outside the Jewish Community, JWV is a staunch supporter of Israel.
In Jacksonville, the Meyer Leibovitz JWV Post is extremely active. The Post participates in
all parades - Veterans Day, July 4th and Memorial Day.
The Group has begun working with the V.A. Hospital in Gainesville and Lake City. They also
collect magazines and supply several hospitals with them.
We also have an active Ladies Auxiliary.
Meetings are held for both the Post and the Auxiliary at Mount Carmel Gardens, on the
second Thursday of the month.
For more information, contact the Quartermaster, Meyer Caplan at 744-2607.

Mr. and Mrs. Club
The Mr. & Mrs. Club, a Jewish Social Club of married couples, ages 30 years and up, has been in existence for 30
years, dances are held every third Saturday night of the month to live band music at the Jacksonville Jewish Center. It
offers socializing in a friendly atmosphere over food and drinks and entertainment is by local or professional talent. This
is climaxed by a giant, gala New Years affair.
Won’t you join us by becoming a member? Call Vice President Carl and Rose Goldberg at 737-8895.

Progressive Credit Union
The Progressive Credit Union was founded in 1940 by two
very splendid men - Laser Klepper and Louis H. Cohen. It was
established to assist their fellow business men and co¬
religionists during the depression years. Hundreds of Jewish
families have benefited by business and personal loans that
were not available to them anywhere else.
The Board of Directors governs the activities of the Credit
Union. They serve without compensation and give their time
and their expertise willingly.
Recently on the occasion of the 46th Annual Meeting the
group chose to honor Moe B. Safer, Board Chairman and Mrs.
Wallace Rubenstein, Board Member, for their many years of
extraordinary services and dedicated efforts through the years
for the Progressive Credit Union.
The Progressive Credit Union offers a great opportunity as a
depository for savings as well as a source for loans. An 8%
dividend on deposits was declared for 1983.

B’nai B’rith, an international service organization founded in
1843, united world Jewry for the advancement of the Jewish
people and helps create a better world for all people. The
needs of the world are great and B’nai B’rith sets an example
to follow. Whether those needs be providing for the poor,
caring for the aged, visiting the sick or incarcerated,
supporting science and art, programming for youth, assisting
victims of natural disasters, making sure Israel lives, or
elevating the mental and moral character of the people of our
faith, B’nai B’rith is more than just a concept, it is living
experience whose resource is people, this vast resource —
people — are giving of themselves to help create an
atmosphere of compassion and understanding. B’nai B’rith is
an organization that opens its arms to all Jewish people and
lets those people gain honor, dignity and authenticity through
programs of educational value, awareness and action.

Magen David
American Red Magen David for
Israel (ARMDI) is the sole authorized
supply and support wing in the
United States of Magen David Adorn
in Israel (MDA). As the nation grows,
as the population expands, as border
problems and other hostilities
continue . . . the demands on the
resources of Magen David Adorn
increase. We are resolved to maintain
the lifesaving services of Magen
David Adorn—with your help!
Founded June 7, 1930, Magen David
Adorn (MDA) was designated Israel’s
official Red Cross service in 1950 by
an act of the Knesset. As the only
emergency medical, blood,
ambulance and disaster service in
Israel, MDA is totally involved in
every aspect of health maintenance
and the preservation of human life.
We must meet Magen David Adom’s
increasing needs with greater
support!
This must be our goal . . .
AND YOU CAN HELP!
MDA BLOOD SERVICES
Magen David Adom’s chief concern
is blood—collecting it, processing it,
storing it and dispensing it to all of
Israel’s medical institutions. MDA
provides 100% of the armed forces
needs and in excess of 85% of the
civilian requirements of this precious
commodity. Headquarters for these
blood services is the Colonel David
Marcus Memorial Institute in Jaffa—
Israel’s largest blood bank and only
blood fractionation plant, which
processes through modern
technology whole blood as well as its
life-giving components: plasma,
gamma globulin, red and white cells,
albumin and fibrinogen. The new
MDA National Blood Service Center
will soon be built in Ramat Gan . . .
AND YOU CAN HELP!
MDA AMBULANCES
Magen David Adorn provides 24-hour
emergency ambulance and coronary
rescue service for all hospitals in
Israel. The fleet of fully-equipped
ambulances is manned by highly
trained doctors and paramedics, who
administer instant emergency
treatment and thus save precious
time needed when life or death
hinges on a few short minutes . . .
AND YOU CAN HELP!
MDA EMERGENCY
MEDICAL CARE CENTERS
Over 200 emergency medical care
centers, substations and underground
Send application to: OLGA WIND - 9640 Wexford Rd. - Jax. 32217
Adorn
shelter clinics are strategically located
throughout Israel. They form a crucial
network of medical services that
renders assistance and saves lives at
all hours of the day and night—at the
scene of an automobile accident,
tending a desperately ill mother,
rushing a child to a hospital, caring for
bombing victims. In any emergency,
Magen David Adorn is there
helping... .

Women’s American Ort
Women’s American Ort is the Organization for Rehabilitation
through Training. Ort is the vocational and technical education of
the Jewish people. For 102 years, since Ort’s inception in Russia,
we have been striving to give man and woman a greater
opportunity in life — given a trade and skill, an individual can
maintain dignity and pride.
Woman’s American Ort is the most complex and one of the
fastest growing Jewish Women’s organizations in the United
States. We are an activist group, not only taking stands, but
positively working to upgrade the quality life for ourselves, our
families, and our communities. We are women who are aware of
the changes that are occuring within our society and are
concerned by the resurgence of global anti-semitism and other
anti-democratic forces which threaten Jewish life, Israel’s survival,
as well as pluralism, tolerance and freedom for all people,
especially Soviet Jewry, and support for Israel and American
Jews.

B’nai B’rith Youth Organization
B’nai B’rith Youth Organization, the largest Jewish youth
organization in the world, is active and growing in the Jacksonville
area. BBYO is comprised of teenagers in grades eight through
twelve and, as an umbrella group, accepts teenagers from all
Jewish sects.
Programs focus upon five major areas: Jewish heritage,
recreation, social, community service and leadership. BBYO’ers
plan their own activities, with advisors acting as chaperones.
The group meets Sunday evenings during the school year, and
plans programs during the summer to stay in touch with members.
If you are interested in joining BBYO, contact Mike Armel or Jami
Goldfarb at 731-3890.
Amity II
The original Amity Club was organized in December, 1951, and
for many years was a great opportunity for the young Jewish
couples in our community to become acquainted and to enjoy a
sociable evening together once a month. It continued for many
years before disbanding.
Feeling the need for an Amity Club again, a group of couples
headed by Sylvia and Izzy Weiss sent fliers out and an open
organizational meeting was held on Februay 17, 1983. At this
meeting, it was agreed to call ourselves Amity II, to have three
events a year including New Years Eve, and that membership be
limited to 135 couples. For information, call Idlene Slaff at 733-
3190.

Whether you’ve reached the top,
or are on your way, you need
One-To-One Banking.
If you are in the stage of life where you
want to protect your assets, having a
Personal Banker isn’t a luxury, it’s a
downright necessity.
One-to-One Banking is the only
approach around that gives you a
banker of your very own. Your
Personal Banker will know you,
your work, your interests, and
most importantly, your banking
needs. Someone to make sure
you’re getting those services
just right for you.
Every time you visit, the same banker
will be there to answer your questions,
offers suggestions, and personally
handle all of your major transactions.
One-to-One is our alternative to the
impersonal bureaucracies of big-
time banking. So visit the Amer¬
ican Bank location nearest you
and sign up for One-to-One
Banking.. .and have a banker
of your very own who will
know you by name - not
account number.

SEW UP
YOUR
It’s surprising how many people
say they are too busy to worry about
the future. . . that they’ll get around to it
when the time comes. A lot of people
believe that Uncle Sam will auto¬
matically provide for such things as
retirement.
There’s only one person you
should be counting on to provide the
financial security your future will
require and that person is you.
Right now is the perfect time to
start sewing up your future with savings
at Citizens Federal Savings and Loan
Association. We’ve got a wide range of
savings accounts geared to your indi¬
vidual needs and goals. The best way
to develop a savings plan that’s right
for you, is to come and talk to us, and
sew up your future today with the sav¬
ings account that suits your needs at
Citizens Federal Savings and Loan
Association.

and Loan Association of Jacksonville
